114 of 1632 DOCUMENTS


People v. Anstey


No. 128368


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


476 Mich. 436; 719 N.W.2d 579; 2006 Mich. LEXIS 1466


March 7, 2006, Argued  
July 31, 2006, Decided  
July 31, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Anstey v. Mich., 127 S. Ct. 976; 166 L. Ed. 2d 740; 2007 U.S. LEXIS 353 (U.S., Jan. 8, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] The Berrien County Trial Court, Alfred M. Butzbaugh, J. The Court of Appeals, ZAHRA, P.J., and NEFF and COOPER, JJ., (Docket No. 255416). The Supreme Court granted the prosecution's application for leave to appeal.
People v. Anstey, 2005 Mich. App. LEXIS 305 (Mich. Ct. App., Feb. 8, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan) that affirmed the trial court judgment that held dismissal was a proper remedy for the denial of defendant's right under Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.625a(6)(d) to an independent chemical test of his bodily alcohol level (BAL) after defendant was arrested for operating under the influence of intoxicating liquor (OUIL) or with an unlawful BAL under Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.625(1).


OVERVIEW: The State challenged the court of appeals decision that held dismissal was the proper remedy when a defendant was denied his right to a reasonable opportunity for an independent BAL chemical test under Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.625a(6)(d). The court found that the text of § 257.625a(6)(d) did not reflect that the Legislature intended either dismissal or suppression of the evidence to be the remedy for a violation of § 257.625a(6)(d); thus the court could not create a remedy that only the Legislature had the power to create. The court held that because § 257.625(d) did not specify a remedy, dismissal or the suppression of the evidence was not a proper remedy for a violation of § 257.625a(6)(d); rather the proper remedy was a permissive instruction informing the jury of the violation and allowing it to determine the significance of that fact. Accordingly the court overruled People v Koval, 371 Mich. 453, 124 N.W.2d 274 (1963), and its progeny, that held dismissal was a proper remedy. The Court also held that defendant's due process right to present a defense was not violated because the police had no constitutional duty to assist defendant in developing potentially exculpatory evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for reinstatement of the charges against defendant. The court noted that the results of the police-administered chemical test would be admissible at trial , but the trial court could instruct the jury that the police violated defendant's statutory right to a reasonable opportunity for an independent chemical test.

 

115 of 1632 DOCUMENTS


Griev. Adm'r v. Fieger


No. 127547


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


476 Mich. 231; 719 N.W.2d 123; 2006 Mich. LEXIS 1470


March 8, 2006, Argued  
July 31, 2006, Decided  
July 31, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay denied by Griev. Adm'r v. Fieger, 477 Mich. 1228; 729 N.W.2d 451; 2006 Mich. LEXIS 3037 (Mich., Dec. 21, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Fieger v. Mi Griev. Adm'r, 127 S. Ct. 1257; 167 L. Ed. 2d 75; 2007 U.S. LEXIS 2081 (U.S., Feb. 20, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] The Attorney Grievance Commission. The Supreme Court granted the application for leave to appeal filed by the Grievance Administrator on behalf of the AGC.
Grievance Adm'r v. Fieger, 609 N.W.2d 184, 2000 Mich. LEXIS 263 (Mich., 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Grievance Administrator sought review of a decision of the Michigan Attorney Discipline Board (ADB), which concluded Mich. Prof. Cond. R. 3.5(c) and 6.5(a) were unconstitutional and remanded for the imposition of an agreed-to professional discipline on appellee attorney. The action surrounded the attorney's derogatory remarks made on his radio show about a three-judge panel that made an adverse ruling in the attorney's malpractice case.


OVERVIEW: The ADB determined that the rules did not apply to the attorney's remarks because they were made outside the courtroom in a case regarded as completed; and if they did apply, they were in violation of the First Amendment. The court reversed and held that the rules were designed to prohibit only undignified, discourteous, and disrespectful conduct or remarks, and not to silence or censor. Further, the case was still pending when the remarks were made because it was during the period in which a motion for rehearing could be filed under Mich. Ct. R. 7.302(C)(2)(c). Indeed, the attorney ultimately did file a timely motion for rehearing. Also, even though made outside a courtroom, the statements attacked the judges in their capacity as judges, and Mich. Prof. Cond. R. 6.5(a) applied as the judges were persons involved in an ongoing legal process. The rules were not vague as there was no question that even the most casual reading of these rules would put a person on notice that the kind of language used by the attorney would violate Mich. Prof. Cond. R. 3.5(c) and 6.5(a). Further, the speech was not political under the First Amendment as there was no political campaign underway.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the opinion and order of the ADB and remanded.

Woodard v. Custer


No. 124994, No. 124995, No. 126275


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


476 Mich. 545; 719 N.W.2d 842; 2006 Mich. LEXIS 1471


December 14, 2005, Argued  
July 31, 2006, Decided  
July 31, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Washtenaw Circuit Court, Timothy P. Connors, J. The Court of Appeals, Meter, P.J., and Talbot and Borrello, JJ., in an unpublished opinion per curiam and in an unpublished opinion concurring in part and dissenting in part by Meter, P.J. (Borrello, J., dissenting in a separate opinion), issued October 21, 2003 (Docket Nos. 239868, 239869) The Supreme Court heard oral argument on whether to grant the applications or take other peremptory action. 471 Mich. 890, 687 N.W.2d 298 (2004). After hearing oral argument, the Supreme Court issued an opinion that concerned only the defendants' application for leave to appeal, in which the Supreme Court reversed the Court of Appeals decision that res ipsa loquitur applied to relieve the plaintiffs of the need to present expert testimony. 473 Mich 1; 702 N.W.2d 522 (2005). The Supreme Court simultaneously granted the plaintiffs' cross-application for leave to appeal the Court of Appeals determination that their proposed expert was not qualified under MCL 600.2169(1). 473 Mich. 856, 701 N.W.2d 133 (2005). Saginaw Circuit Court, William A. Crane, J. The Court of Appeals, O'Connell, P.J., and Jansen and Murray, JJ. 261 Mich. App. 608, 684 N.W.2d 366 (2004).  [***2] The Supreme Court granted the defendant's application for leave to appeal. 473 Mich. 858, 701 N.W.2d 134 (2005).
Hamilton v. Kuligowski, 261 Mich. App. 608, 684 N.W.2d 366, 2004 Mich. App. LEXIS 1021 (2004)
Woodward v. Custer, 2003 Mich. App. LEXIS 2647 (Mich. Ct. App., Oct. 21, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A trial court held that two experts in two medical malpractice cases filed by plaintiffs, parents of an infant and the personal representative of a decedent against defendant physicians, were not qualified as experts under Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.2169. The Court of Appeals of Michigan affirmed the decision in the first case but reversed in the second. The physicians appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents sued the physician, alleging that the infant's legs were fractured as a result of negligent medical procedures. The personal representative sued a second physician alleging that he failed to properly diagnose and treat her while exhibiting stroke symptoms. On appeal, the court held that the parents' expert was not qualified under § 600.2169 because: (1) pediatric critical care was the one most relevant specialty, as the infant was critically ill when the procedures were performed, and the expert did not specialize in pediatric critical care medicine at the time of the alleged malpractice and had never specialized in pediatric critical care medicine; (2) the expert was not board-certified in pediatric critical care medicine; and (3) during the year immediately preceding the alleged malpractice, the expert did not practice or teach pediatric critical care medicine. The personal representative's expert was not qualified under § 600.2169 because the physician specialized in general internal medicine and was practicing general internal medicine, and during the year immediately preceding the alleged malpractice the expert devoted his time to treating infectious diseases.


OUTCOME: The judgment in the first case was affirmed but was reversed in the second case and the case was remanded to the trial court for reentry of its order granting the physician a directed verdict.

People v. Derror


No. 129269, No. 129364


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


475 Mich. 316; 715 N.W.2d 822; 2006 Mich. LEXIS 1205


January 10, 2006, Argued  
June 21, 2006, Decided  
June 21, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Grand Traverse Circuit Court, Philip E. Rogers, J. Jackson Circuit Court, Chad C. Schmucker, J. The Court of Appeals, Cooper, P.J., and Jansen and Hoekstra, JJ. The Supreme Court granted both applications and ordered that the cases be submitted together.
People v. Derror, 268 Mich. App. 67, 706 N.W.2d 451, 2005 Mich. App. LEXIS 2161 (2005).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed judgments of the Court of Appeals of Michigan in two consolidated cases holding that 11-carboxy-THC was not a schedule one controlled substance under Mich. Comp. Laws § 333.7212 in defendants' criminal cases charging them with driving under the influence under Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.625(8).


OVERVIEW: Defendants, in two different cases, were charged with operating a motor vehicle with the presence of a schedule one controlled substance in their bodies in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.625(8). Both admitted to having smoked marijuana before their auto accidents, and blood tests showed the presence of 11-carboxy-THC, a by-product or metabolite of marijuana. On appeal of the appellate court's decision, the court held that because 11-carboxy-THC qualified as a derivative, and since derivatives were included within the definition of marijuana, which Mich. Comp. Laws § 333.7212(1)(c) specifically listed as a schedule one controlled substance, 11-carboxy-THC was a schedule one controlled substance under § 333.7212(1)(c) for the purpose of Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.625(8). The court further held that Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.625(4), (5), and (8) did not require proof of a defendant's knowledge of his or her intoxication.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. McCuller


No. 128161


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


475 Mich. 176; 715 N.W.2d 798; 2006 Mich. LEXIS 1199



June 13, 2006, Decided  
June 13, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Vacated by, Remanded by, Motion granted by McCuller v. Michigan, 127 S. Ct. 1247, 167 L. Ed. 2d 62, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 2002 (U.S., 2007)
Later proceeding at People v. McCuller, 477 Mich. 1288, 2007 Mich. LEXIS 1005 (2007)
On remand at, Reaffirmed People v. McCuller, 2007 Mich. LEXIS 1628 (Mich., July 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Oakland Circuit Court, Richard D. Kuhn, J. The Court of Appeals, Talbot, P.J., and Griffin and Wilder, JJ. (Docket No. 250000). The Supreme Court, in lieu of granting leave to appeal, ordered oral argument on whether to grant the defendant's application for leave to appeal. 474 Mich. 925, 706 N.W.2d 11 (2005).
People v. McCuller, 2005 Mich. App. LEXIS 37 (Mich. Ct. App., Jan. 11, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court, in lieu of granting leave to appeal, ordered oral argument on whether to grant defendant's application for leave to appeal a judgment of the Oakland Circuit Court (Michigan) that sentenced him to 2 to 15 years in prison upon his conviction for assault with intent to do great bodily harm less than murder under Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.84. Defendant claimed he was entitled to an intermediate sentence under Mich. Comp. Laws § 769.34(4)(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed he was entitled to an intermediate sanction, rather than a prison term, because his prior record variable (PRV) score alone placed him in a recommended minimum guidelines range of 0 to 11 months, which was within the 18 month upper limit for an intermediate sentence under Mich. Comp. Laws § 769.34(4)(a). Defendant also claimed that the trial court violated the Blakely rule by engaging in judicial fact-finding to score the offense variables (OVs). The court noted that Mich. Comp. Laws § 777.21 explicitly required the trial court to consider the OVs, the PRVs, and the offense class to determine a defendant's recommended minimum guidelines range. The court held that when defendant's OVs, PRVs, and offense class were considered, his minimum sentence range was 5 to 28 months; thus he was not entitled to an intermediate sanction under Mich. Comp. Laws § 769.34(4)(a). The court held that the trial court did not violate the Blakely rule by scoring the OVs before imposing a prison sentence within the guidelines, and that its holding was consistent with Ring v. Arizona because defendant's statutory maximum sentence was not increased on the basis of judicial findings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence. The court denied defendant's application for appeal in all other respects because the court was not persuaded that it should review the remaining questions presented.

City of Taylor v. Detroit Edison Co.


No. 127580


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


475 Mich. 109; 715 N.W.2d 28; 2006 Mich. LEXIS 999


March 7, 2006, Argued  
May 31, 2006, Decided  
May 31, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wayne Circuit Court. John A. Murphy, J. The Court of Appeals, Murphy, P.J., and Griffin and White, JJ. The Supreme Court granted the defendant's application for leave to appeal.
City of Taylor v. Detroit Edison Co., 263 Mich. App. 551, 689 N.W.2d 482, 2004 Mich. App. LEXIS 2365 (2004).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant utility appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed in part a decision of the circuit court granting summary disposition in favor of plaintiff city in the city's action seeking a declaratory judgment that the utility was obligated to pay the entire cost to relocate wires under Taylor, Mich., Ord. 00-344.


OVERVIEW: Court of appeals determined that the Michigan Public Service Commission (MPSC) did not have primary jurisdiction and that the city exercised a governmental function and properly required the utility to bear the cost of relocation. On review, the court reversed. Although Mich. Const. art. 7, §§ 22, 29 gave general authority to the city, the authority was subject to the constitution and law. The legislature created the MPSC under Mich. Comp. Laws § 460.6 and gave it broad regulatory authority over public utilities. The court deferred to the MPSC and its primary jurisdiction on the question as to whether the city's ordinance conflicted with MPSC regulations. The court reaffirmed the standard that a municipality could regulate highways, streets, alleys, and public places to the degree such regulations were consistent with state law. The court did agree that the MPSC had no jurisdiction to consider the scope of the city's constitutional authority.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals and remanded to the circuit court to grant summary disposition to the power company.

Wexford Med. Group v. City of Cadillac


No. 127152


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


474 Mich. 192; 713 N.W.2d 734; 2006 Mich. LEXIS 907


November 9, 2005, Argued  
May 4, 2006, Decided  
May 3, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Tax Tribunal. The Court of Appeals, SMOLENSKI, P.J., and WHITE and KELLY, JJ. (Docket No. 250197). The Supreme Court granted the petitioner's application for leave to appeal. 472 Mich. 899; 696 N.W.2d 708 (2005).
McLaren Reg. Med. Ctr. v. City of Owosso, 2004 Mich. App. LEXIS 2265 (Mich. Ct. App., Aug. 24, 2004)



DISPOSITION:  The judgment was reversed insofar as it held that the corporation was not a charitable institution. The judgment was vacated insofar as it held that the corporation did not exist for a public health purpose. The case was remanded to the Tax Tribunal for entry of judgment for the corporation.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner nonprofit corporation appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals of Michigan holding that the corporation was not a charitable institution under Mich. Comp. Laws §§ 211.7o, 211.9(a) and that the corporation did not exist for a public health purpose under Mich. Comp. Laws § 211.7r, after the corporation challenged property taxes assessed by respondent city.


OVERVIEW: The corporation provided free and discounted health care to anyone whose income was up to twice the federal poverty level. After the corporation challenged the city's assessment of property taxes, both the Tax Tribunal and the appellate court held that the corporation was not a charity and therefore was not entitled a tax exemption. On appeal, the court reversed. Both the Tax Tribunal and the appellate court misapplied existing law by erroneously narrowing the focus of their inquiry to the value of the free medical care the corporation rendered in the given tax years. The corporation was a charitable institution under Mich. Comp. Laws §§ 211.7o, 211.9(a) because it existed for, and carried out, the purpose of giving a gift for the benefit of an indefinite number of persons by providing free and below-cost medical care to anyone who needed it without qualification, and it realized no pecuniary gain from its activities. Therefore it was entitled to an ad valorem tax exemption.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed insofar as it held that the corporation was not a charitable institution. The judgment was vacated insofar as it held that the corporation did not exist for a public health purpose. The case was remanded to the Tax Tribunal for entry of judgment for the corporation.

People v. Gillis


No. 127194


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


474 Mich. 105; 712 N.W.2d 419; 2006 Mich. LEXIS 624


October 18, 2005, Argued  
April 5, 2006, Decided  
April 5, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at People v. Gillis, 2006 Mich. App. LEXIS 1817 (Mich. Ct. App., June 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] St. Clair Circuit Court, James P. Adair, J. Court of Appeals, Jansen, P.J., and Cooper, J. (Meter, J., concurring in part and dissenting in part), (Docket No. 245012). The Supreme Court granted the prosecution's application for leave to appeal.
People v. Gillis, 2004 Mich. App. LEXIS 2176 (Mich. Ct. App., Aug. 17, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which vacated defendant's convictions of first-degree felony murder under Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.316(1)(b), with home invasion in the first degree, Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.110a, as the predicate felony. The Court of Appeals concluded that the automobile accident that killed the victims was not part of the continuous transaction of or immediately connected to the home invasion.


OVERVIEW: A homeowner confronted defendant in the doorway of his home and defendant fled in his car. An officer gave chase, then defendant's vehicle had a head-on collision with the victims. The court reversed and held that "perpetration" as used in the felony-murder statute contemplated something beyond the definitional elements of the predicate felony. The court concluded that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for a directed verdict of acquittal because a reasonable juror could conclude that defendant was still in the midst of his escape from the home invasion when he struck the victims. The scene of the murders was sufficiently close in both time and distance from the scene of the home invasion. Also, the trial court did not err in failing to instruct on involuntary manslaughter because no rational juror could conclude that defendant's actions were anything other than acts that created a very high risk of death or great bodily harm with knowledge that death or great bodily harm was the probable result, given that defendant knowingly entered an interstate highway going the wrong way.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and remanded the case to the court of appeals.

Devillers v. Auto Club Ins. Ass'n


No. 126899


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


473 Mich. 562; 702 N.W.2d 539; 2005 Mich. LEXIS 1313


April 12, 2005, Argued  
July 29, 2005, Decided  
July 29, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Oakland Circuit Court, Nanci J. Grant, J. Court of Appeals, FITZGERALD, P.J., and GAGE and COOPER, JJ. (Docket No. 257449). Supreme Court granted leave to appeal. 471 Mich. 923, 689 N.W.2d 227 (2004).
Devillers v. A.C.I.A., 471 Mich. 923, 689 N.W.2d 227, 2004 Mich. LEXIS 2653 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Oakland Circuit Court, Michigan, denied defendant insurer's motion for partial summary judgment on plaintiff mother's complaint seeking payment for services allegedly rendered for which she did not receive payment. The Michigan Court of Appeals denied the insurer's leave to appeal, which was subsequently granted by the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: The insurer asked that the supreme court overrule a prior case and apply as written the "one-year-back" limitation provided for in Mich. Comp. Laws § 500.3145(1) for recovering no-fault personal protection insurance benefits. The supreme court found there was a plainly expressed legislative intent that recovery of personal injury protection (PIP) be limited to losses incurred within the year prior to the filing of the lawsuit. The mother had a full year following the February 2001 termination of payment for home health-care benefits within which to seek reimbursement. The mother's ability to file suit was not thwarted by dilatory tactics on the part of the insurer or by the exercise of the insurer's right to delay payment for 30 days following receipt of proof of loss. The supreme court's decision was to be given retroactive effect and was applicable to all pending cases. There was no allegation of fraud, mutual mistake, or any other unusual circumstance; thus, there was no basis to invoke the supreme court's equitable power. Therefore, the mother's claim was barred by the one-year back rule.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded for entry of an order of partial summary disposition in favor of the insurer.

Glass v. Goeckel


No. 126409


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


473 Mich. 667; 703 N.W.2d 58; 2005 Mich. LEXIS 1314


March 8, 2005, Argued  
July 29, 2005, Decided  
July 29, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Glass v. Goeckel, 703 N.W.2d 188, 2005 Mich. LEXIS 1520 (Mich., 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Goeckel v. Glass, 126 S. Ct. 1340; 164 L. Ed. 2d 54; 2006 U.S. LEXIS 1200 (U.S., Feb. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Alcona Circuit Court, John F. Kowalski, J. Court of Appeals, O'CONNELL, P.J., and WILDER and MURRAY, JJ., 262 Mich. App. 29; 683 N.W.2d 719 (2004). Supreme Court granted leave to appeal. 471 Mich. 904; 688 N.W.2d 91 (2004).
Glass v. Goeckel, 262 Mich. App. 29, 683 N.W.2d 719, 2004 Mich. App. LEXIS 1229 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of plaintiff in her action to enjoin defendant property owners from interfering with her walking along the shoreline of one of the Great Lakes in an area where defendants owned property and their deed defined a boundary as the meander line of the lake.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals held that the state held title to previously submerged land, subject to the exclusive use of the riparian owner up to the water's edge and that no member of the public had a right to traverse the land between the statutory ordinary high water mark and the literal water's edge. The court noted that the public trust doctrine applied to the great lakes and reversed the judgment of the court of appeals. The court held that the Great Lakes Submerged Lands Act (GLSLA), Mich. Comp. Laws § 324.32501 et seq., reiterated the state's authority as trustee of the inalienable jus publicum, which extended over both publicly and privately owned lands and that the GLSLA made no claims to alter the delineation of the jus privatum of individual landowners, although the two could overlap. The court of appeals erred by granting defendants exclusive right of use down to the water's edge because littoral property remained subject to the public trust and their rights superseded public rights only to the extent that they did not contravene the public trust. The court concluded that plaintiff could walk the shores of the lake below the ordinary high water mark.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals.


 

126 of 1632 DOCUMENTS



Rory v. Cont'l Ins. Co.


No. 126747


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


473 Mich. 457; 703 N.W.2d 23; 2005 Mich. LEXIS 1311


March 8, 2005, Argued  
July 28, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wayne Circuit Court, Robert L. Ziolkowski, J. Court of Appeals, BORRELLO, P.J., and WHITE and SMOLENSKI, JJ. Supreme Court granted the defendants' application for leave to appeal.
Rory v. Cont'l Ins. Co., 262 Mich. App. 679, 687 N.W.2d 304, 2004 Mich. App. LEXIS 1862 (2004)



DISPOSITION: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed the trial court's refusal to enforce the one-year contractual limitations period contained in the insurance policy issue to plaintiff insureds in plaintiffs' action to recover uninsured motorist (UIM) benefits.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were involved in an accident and did not discover that the other driver was uninsured until suit was filed, which was more than a year after the accident. Defendant denied their claim UIM benefits because the policy required the claim to be filed within one year after the accident. The trial court held that the one-year limitations period was unreasonable and that it was an unenforceable adhesion clause. The court reversed and held that an unambiguous provision providing for a shortened period of limitation was enforceable unless it would violate law or public policy. The court also held that Mich. Comp. Laws § 500.2254 did not bar the imposition of conditions that may be placed on the commencement and maintenance of a lawsuit. The state insurance commissioner had approved the insurer's policy form containing the shortened limitations provision for issuance and use in the State of Michigan. Further, an adhesion contract was simply a type of contract to be enforced as any other contract and plaintiffs did not allege that they were fraudulently induced to sign the agreement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals.


 

127 of 1632 DOCUMENTS


People v. Schaefer


No. 126067, No. 127142


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


473 Mich. 418; 703 N.W.2d 774; 2005 Mich. LEXIS 1190


May 10, 2005, Argued  
July 27, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Schaefer--Wayne Circuit Court, Leonard Townsend, J. Court of Appeals, BORRELLO, P.J. and WHITE, J. (SMOLENSKI, J., dissenting) (Docket No. 245175). Large--2th District Court, Lysle G. Hall, J. Court of Appeals, MURRAY, P.J., and MARKEY and O'CONNELL, JJ. (Docket No. 253261).
People v. Schaefer, 2004 Mich. App. LEXIS 831 (Mich. Ct. App., Mar. 25, 2004)
People v. Large, 2004 Mich. App. LEXIS 2097 (Mich. Ct. App., Aug. 10, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, defendants challenged decisions of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed their convictions for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of liquor and causing death (OUIL causing death), under Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.625(4). The court revisited its decision in People v Lardie, 452 Mich. 231 (1996).


OVERVIEW: Defendant one had a 0.16 blood-alcohol level (BAL), was driving erratically, and had an accident that killed the passenger. Defendant two had a .10 BAL, and hit and killed a girl on a bicycle. The court held that the Lardie court's reliance on policy considerations in construing Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.625(4) was misplaced and that § 257.625(4) plainly required that the victim's death be caused by defendant's operation of the vehicle, not defendant's intoxicated operation. As to defendant one, any error of the trial court in merely reading the statute and failing to explain the causation element of OUIL causing death was harmless, but the case was remanded for a determination as to whether the trial court committed reversible error by referring to defendant's stipulation as to his BAL. As to defendant two, the issue of causation was less certain because while there was evidence that the victim's death was the direct result of defendant's operation of the vehicle, the victim rode a bicycle without brakes down a hill onto a busy road. The court overturned Laridie to the extent that it held that a defendant's intoxicated driving must be a substantial cause of the vicitm's death.


OUTCOME: As to defendant one, the court vacated the judgment and remanded to address defendant's remaining argument. As to defendant two, the court reversed and remanded for reconsideration of whether to bind defendant over on the charge of OUIL causing death in light of the principles set forth in this opinion.

 

128 of 1632 DOCUMENTS



City of Novi v. Robert Adell Children's Funded Trust


No. 122985


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


473 Mich. 242; 701 N.W.2d 144; 2005 Mich. LEXIS 1136


April 13, 2005, Argued  
July 20, 2005, Decided  
July 20, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Oakland Circuit Court, Jessica R. Cooper, J. Court of Appeals, WHITBECK, C.J., and O'CONNELL and METER, JJ. 253 Mich App 330; 659 N.W.2d 615 (2002). Supreme Court granted the city's application for leave to appeal. 471 Mich 889; 687 N.W.2d 297 (2004).
City of Novi v. Robert Adell Children's Funded Trust, 253 Mich. App. 330, 659 N.W.2d 615, 2002 Mich. App. LEXIS 1379 (2002).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city sought to take defendant private property owners' land to construct a road. The owners filed a motion challenging the public purpose and necessity of the taking pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 213.56 of Michigan's Uniform Condemnation Procedures Act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 231.51 et seq. The trial court concluded that the proposed taking was unconstitutional, and the Michigan Court of Appeals affirmed. The city sought review.


OVERVIEW: On review, the city contended that the "spur road" part of the project constituted a public use and that the property owners did not successfully challenge the necessity of the project. The supreme court agreed, finding that the city initiated the project in response to growing traffic problems, and that ownership, control, and maintenance would remain with the city. The public would be free to use the spur, and although a nearby business would be the primary user of the spur, it was the right of travel by all the world, and not the exercise of the right, which made the spur a public highway. The business was to be granted no interest in the property and would have no ability to control access to the road. As such, the supreme court found that the proposed project was a public road, and thus a public use; thus, the lower courts erred in ruling otherwise. Contrary to the owners' assertions, fraud did not provide them a basis for relief because the requisite elements were not supported by the record. Further, the city was not obligated to show that its plan was the best or only alternative, only that it was a reasonable one; the owners did not show that the plan was unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The decision that the proposed road was not a public use was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for entry of summary disposition in favor of the city.


 

129 of 1632 DOCUMENTS



Studier v. Mich. Pub. Sch. Emples. Ret. Bd.


No. 125765, No. 125766


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


472 Mich. 642; 698 N.W.2d 350; 2005 Mich. LEXIS 925; 35 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2453


January 12, 2005, Argued  
June 28, 2005, Decided  
June 28, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Ingham Circuit Court, Lawrence M. Glazer, J. Court of Appeals, FITZGERALD, P.J., and NEFF and WHITE, JJ. 260 Mich App 460, 679 N.W.2d 88 (2004). Supreme Court granted leave to appeal on applications by the plaintiffs and the defendants. 471 Mich 875, 688 N.W.2d 500 (2004).
Studier v. Mich. Pub. Sch. Emples. Ret. Bd., 260 Mich. App. 460, 679 N.W.2d 88, 2004 Mich. App. LEXIS 317 (2004).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, public school retirees, sought review of a decision from the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which ruled in favor of defendant state agencies in a challenge to the validity of health care copay and deductible increases.


OVERVIEW: The retirees alleged that the copay and deductible increases violated Mich. Const. art. 9, § 24, which prohibited the state or a political subdivision from diminishing or impairing the accrued financial benefits of any pension plan or retirement system it offered. The retirees further alleged that the increases resulted from a law that impaired an existing contractual obligation in violation of Mich. Const. art. 1, § 10 and U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. The court held that health care benefits were not protected by Mich. Const. art. 9, § 24 because they were not accrued benefits or financial benefits as those terms were commonly understood at the time of ratification; thus, they did not constitute accrued financial benefits. The court further held that Mich. Comp. Laws § 38.1391(1) did not give public school employees a contractual right to health care benefits because the plain language of the statute did not clearly indicate that the legislature intended to surrender its legislative powers through the statute's enactment. Accordingly, there was no impairment of a contractual obligation because no contractual relationship with the retirees existed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of appeals' determination that health care benefits did not constitute accrued financial benefits, reversed the court of appeals' conclusion that a contractual relationship with the retirees existed, and affirmed the court of appeals' determination that the circuit court properly entered summary disposition in the agencies' favor.

Twp. of Casco v. Sec'y of State


No. 126120, No. 126369


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


472 Mich. 566; 701 N.W.2d 102; 2005 Mich. LEXIS 886


March 8, 2005, Argued  
June 14, 2005, Decided  
June 14, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Fillmore Twp. v. Sec'y of State, 473 Mich. 1205; 699 N.W.2d 697; 2005 Mich. LEXIS 1307 (Mich., July 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Ingham Circuit Court, Peter D. Houk, J. Court of Appeals, COOPER and CAVANAGH, JJ. (ZAHRA, P.J., dissenting), affirmed. Court of Appeals, GRIFFIN, P.J., and METER and SCHUETTE, JJ. (Docket No. 245640).
Fillmore Twp. v. Sec'y of State, 471 Mich. 890, 688 N.W.2d 281, 2004 Mich. LEXIS 1911 (2004)
Twp. of Casco v. Sec'y of State, 261 Mich. App. 386, 682 N.W.2d 546, 2004 Mich. App. LEXIS 804 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, plaintiffs, townships and residents of those townships who sought to detach territory from defendant cities, sought review of decisions from the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which denied mandamus relief to compel state approval of detachment elections.


OVERVIEW: In one case, the proposed election would have allowed residents of one township to vote on a change in the boundaries of another township in which they did not reside. In the other case, the petition involved an effort to detach territory for addition to more than one township. The court held that the refusal to certify the petitions was proper because a petition and a vote about detachment could involve only one city and one township. Pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws §§ 117.6, 117.8(1), and 117.11(2), detachment had to be approved by qualified electors, as defined in Mich. Comp. Laws § 168.10, of the district to be affected, as defined in Mich. Comp. Laws § 117.9(1). Thus, residents of one township were not qualified electors in a detachment proceeding with respect to determining a change of boundaries for another township. The language of Mich. Comp. Laws § 117.13 also suggested that the district to be affected could comprise only one city and one township. Moreover, combining multiple additions of territory in a single detachment petition so that there was only a single vote violated the prohibition of Mich. Comp. Laws § 168.643a against combining independent propositions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decisions of the court of appeals.

132 of 1632 DOCUMENTS


People v. Shepherd


No. 127303


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


472 Mich. 343; 697 N.W.2d 144; 2005 Mich. LEXIS 593



May 24, 2005, Decided  
May 24, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Midland Circuit Court, Thomas L. Ludington, J. Court of Appeals, COOPER and KELLY, JJ. (HOEKSTRA, P.J., dissenting). 263 Mich App 665; 689 N.W.2d 721 (2004).
People v. Shepherd, 263 Mich. App. 665; 689 N.W.2d 721; 2004 Mich. App. LEXIS 2501 (2004).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted and sentenced in the Midland Circuit Court, Michigan, for the offense of perjury. The Michigan Court of Appeals reversed her conviction on the basis that there was constitutional error in admitting evidence of a transcript of an unavailable witness's testimony from a different case. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: At defendant's trial, the trial court admitted the transcript of the hearing at which her boyfriend pleaded guilty of subornation of perjury. Also admitted were certain statements that the boyfriend made while in jail, a script of questions and answers that he had created for defendant in preparation for her testimony in his fleeing and eluding trial, and the testimony of witnesses who were present on the morning of the fleeing and eluding offense. The court of appeals found constitutional error in the admission of the plea transcript, and that it was not at all clear that a rational jury would have found defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt absent the improperly admitted statement. On appeal, the State argued that although the plea transcript was improperly admitted, the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The supreme court held that on the basis of the overwhelming evidence of the falsity of defendant's testimony in the fleeing and eluding trial, it was clear beyond a reasonable doubt that a reasonable jury would have found her guilty of perjury even if the transcript of her boyfriend's plea to the charge of subornation of perjury had not been admitted.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was reversed, and the matter remanded to the trial court for the reinstatement of defendant's conviction and the sentence.

Warda v. City Council


No. 125561


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


472 Mich. 326; 696 N.W.2d 671; 2005 Mich. LEXIS 589



May 18, 2005, Decided  
May 18, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Genesee Circuit Court, James T. Corden, J. Court of Appeals, O'CONNELL, P.J., and WILDER, J. (JANSEN, J., dissenting) (Docket No. 241188).
Warda v. City Council of Flushing, 2003 Mich. App. LEXIS 3396 (Mich. Ct. App., Dec. 23, 2003).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city council appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed the circuit court's decision for plaintiff police officer in his declaratory action contending that the city abused its discretion in denying his request for attorney fees to defend himself against criminal prosecution for what the officer contended was within the scope of his duty as an employee with the city.


OVERVIEW: The officer was certified to inspect salvage vehicles and was charged with falsifying a certification under Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.903, and acquitted. The issue was whether the judiciary had the authority to review the city council's denial of the officer's request for reimbursement. The court held that the State, through § 8 of the governmental immunity act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 691.1408, had clearly conferred upon the city council the power which it exercised and left the exercise of it to the judgment and discretion of the council. Whether the council acted wisely or unwisely, prudently or imprudently, was not for the consideration or determination of the court. The officer did not suggest that the city council's decision was unconstitutional in any way. Nor was there any evidence in the record that would suggest such unconstitutionality. In overruling Exeter Township Clerk v. Exeter Township Board, 108 Mich. App. 262, 108 Mich. App. 262, and Bowens v. City of Pontiac, 165 Mich. App. 416, the court held that absent a showing that the governmental agency exercised its discretion in an unconstitutional manner, the court was without the power to review such decisions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Court of Appeals.


 

134 of 1632 DOCUMENTS



Associated Builders & Contrs. v. Wilbur


No. 124835


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


472 Mich. 117; 693 N.W.2d 374; 2005 Mich. LEXIS 275



March 9, 2005, Decided  
March 9, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at Associated Builders & Contrs. v. Dir., Dep't of Consumer & Indus. Servs., 267 Mich. App. 386, 705 N.W.2d 509, 2005 Mich. App. LEXIS 1719 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Associated Builders & Contrs. v. Wilbur, 2003 Mich. App. LEXIS 1855 (Mich. Ct. App., Aug. 5, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Decision of Court of Appeals reversed; remanded to Court of Appeals for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trade association brought an action for declaratory and injunctive relief, challenging the constitutionality of the Michigan Prevailing Wage Act (PWA). The Michigan Court of Appeals reversed the circuit court's denial of the governmental defendants' motion for summary disposition of the claim of unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority and affirmed the dismissal of the association's vagueness claim. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The association argued that the PWA was unconstitutionally vague and constituted an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority to unions and union contractors. The appellate court concluded that the association could not seek declaratory relief because it had alleged no "actual controversy" under the court rule governing declaratory judgments, Mich. Ct. R. 2.605. However, the instant court held that the association presented an "actual controversy" and could seek declaratory relief under Rule 2.605. The association was not required to submit evidence of a threat of imminent prosecution in order to establish standing. It was sufficient to establish standing that the association's members were directly regulated by the PWA and were required to conform their pay and benefit practices to that of union contractors on state-funded projects. The affidavits submitted by the association articulated concrete risks of violations of the PWA. The risks of enforcement of the PWA, together with the asserted character of the potential for violations of the PWA, presented a justiciable controversy.


OUTCOME: The instant court reversed the appellate court's denial of declaratory relief and remanded to that court for reconsideration and resolution of defendants' appeal and the association's cross-appeal on the merits.

Nat'l Wildlife Fed'n v. Cleveland Cliffs Iron Co.


Docket No. 121890.


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


471 Mich. 608; 684 N.W.2d 800; 2004 Mich. LEXIS 1695


January 13, 2004, Argued  
July 30, 2004, Decided  
July 30, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Updated Copy March 4, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Marquette Circuit Court, Garfield W. Hood, J. Court of Appeals, GRIFFIN, P.J., and HOOD and SAWYER, JJ. (Docket No. 232706).
NATIONAL WILDLIFE FEDN. & UPPER PENINSULA ENVTL. COALITION v. CLEVELAND CLIFFS IRON CO, 2002 Mich. App. LEXIS 829 (Mich. Ct. App., June 11, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Decision of Court of Appeals affirmed; remanded to trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mining companies sought review of a decision from the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which reversed the trial court's ruling that plaintiff environmental groups lacked standing to bring a suit on behalf of their members under the Michigan Environmental Protection Act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 324.1701 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The complaint alleged illegal discharges of pollutants into a river. The court of appeals ruled that the environmental groups had standing to seek injunctive relief as a remedy under Mich. Comp. Laws § 324.1704(1). In affirming, the court emphasized the importance of standing as an aspect of the judicial power under Mich. Const. art. 6, § 1 and of separation of powers under Mich. Const. art. 3, § 2. The court found that the environmental groups sufficiently asserted injury to their members by averring that they used the affected area and were persons for whom the aesthetic and recreational values of the area would be lessened by the challenged activity. Such averments were adequate to allege injury in fact. The environmental groups also provided an affidavit from an expert, which discussed the effects of the pollution on groundwater flow, recharge rate, stream flow, and water quality, as well as the expected effects on birds, fish, and plants from habitat destruction. Because the court ruled that the environmental groups had standing without regard to Mich. Comp. Laws § 324.1701(1), the court declined to address the constitutionality of the standing provisions of § 1701(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

County of Wayne v. Hathcock


No. 124070, No. 124071, No. 124072, No. 124073, No. 124074, No. 124075, No. 124076, No. 124077, No. 124078


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


471 Mich. 445; 684 N.W.2d 765; 2004 Mich. LEXIS 1693


April 21, 2004, Argued  
July 30, 2004, Decided  
July 30, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Updated Copy March 4, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wayne Circuit Court, Michael F. Sapala, J., Court of Appeals, O'CONNELL, P.J., and MURRAY, and FITZGERALD, JJ., in an unpublished opinion per curiam, a concurring opinion by MURRAY, J., and an opinion by FITZGERALD, J., concurring with MURRAY, J., affirmed. MURRAY and FITZGERALD, JJ. (Docket Nos. 239438, 239563, 240184, 240187, 240189, 240190, 240193-240195).
COUNTY OF WAYNE v. HATHCOCK, 2003 Mich. App. LEXIS 1042 (Mich. Ct. App., Apr. 24, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owners appealed a decision from the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed the trial court's judgment upholding plaintiff county's determination of necessity in an eminent domain case.


OVERVIEW: The county sought to condemn the property owners' land for the construction of a large business and technology park. The court found that the county was authorized to condemn property under Mich. Comp. Laws § 213.23 and that the creation of jobs was a public purpose within its authority. The county's charter provision regarding its authority, Wayne County, Mich., Charter § 1.112, fell within the scope of its home rule powers under Mich. Const. art. 7, §§ 1, 2, 34 and Mich. Comp. Laws § 45.515(c). The lack of an identified purchaser did not defeat a finding of necessity. The court concluded, however, that the proposed condemnation did not pass constitutional muster because the taking was not for public use within the meaning of Mich. Const. art. 10, § 2. The park was not an enterprise dependent on the use of land that could be assembled only by government action. The park would not be subject to public oversight after being sold to private entities. There were no facts of independent public significance, such as health and safety issues, that might justify the condemnation. In so holding, the court overruled Poletown Neighborhood Council v. Detroit, 410 Mich. 616 (1981).


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for entry of an order of summary disposition in the property owners' favor.

Taxpayers of Mich. Against Casinos v. State


No. 122830


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


471 Mich. 306; 685 N.W.2d 221; 2004 Mich. LEXIS 1700


March 11, 2004, Argued  
July 30, 2004, Decided  
July 30, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Updated Copy March 3, 2005.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Taxpayers of Mich. Against Casinos v. Michigan, 543 U.S. 1146; 161 L. Ed. 2d 106, 125 S. Ct. 1298, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 1470 (U.S., 2005)
On remand at, Remanded by Taxpayers of Mich. Against Casinos v. State, 268 Mich. App. 226; 708 N.W.2d 115; 2005 Mich. App. LEXIS 2246 (Mich. Ct. App., Sept. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Ingham Circuit Court, Peter D. Houk, J. Court of Appeals, HOOD, P.J., and HOLBROOK, JR., and OWENS, JJ. 254 Mich App 23, 657 N.W.2d 503 (2002).
Taxpayers of Mich. Against Casinos v. Michigan, 254 Mich. App. 23, 657 N.W.2d 503, 2002 Mich. App. LEXIS 1562 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Decision of Court of Appeals affirmed in part; remanded to the Court of Appeals for further consideration.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff anti-casino taxpayer group appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which reversed a circuit court decision and held that the Legislature's approval by resolution rather than by a bill of tribal-state gaming compacts under the Indian Gaming Regulatory Act, 25 U.S.C.S. § 2701 et seq., did not violate Mich. Const. art. 4, § 22 and that the resolution was not a "local act" in violation of Mich. Const. art. 4, § 29.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs challenged the court of appeals decision that held the Michigan Legislature's approval of the gaming compacts by resolution was not constitutionally infirm. The court held that the compacts were contracts and did not constitute legislation, as they contained no enforcement provision and the power of the state to legislate in this area was preempted by federal law. The court also found that the compacts did not impose any affirmative obligations on the state, create rules of conduct for Michigan citizens, or create new state agencies. The court held that the Legislature did not modify Michigan law, but merely expressed its approval of valid contracts between two independent, sovereign entities. The court also agreed that the resolution was not a "local act." The court affirmed the judgment, but remanded plaintiffs' claim as to the compacts' amendment provision, because the court of appeals had found the issue was not ripe for review, but the Governor had since invoked the provision, and the lower courts had not yet reviewed the issue of whether it violated the separation of powers doctrine in Mich. Const. art. 3, § 2 by allowing amendment without legislative approval.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of appeals judgment that held the tribal-state gaming compacts were not legislation and could be approved by resolution rather than by a bill and that the resolution was not a local act. The court remanded the issue of whether the amendatory provision of the compacts violated the separation of powers doctrine.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Kreiner: Lapeer Circuit Court, Nick O. Holowka, J. Court of Appeals, WHITE, P.J., and MURPHY and FITZGERALD, JJ. 251 Mich. App. 513, 651 N.W.2d 433 (2002). Supreme Court. 468 Mich. 885, 661 N.W.2d 234 (2003). Court of Appeals. 256 Mich. App. 680, 671 N.W.2d 95 (2003). Straub: Monroe Circuit Court, Michael W. LaBeau, J. Court of Appeals, HOOD, P.J., and SMOLENSKI and KELLY, JJ. 254 Mich. App. 454, 657 N.W.2d 178 (2002). Supreme Court. 468 Mich. 920, 664 N.W.2d 212 (2003). Court of Appeals, SMOLENSKI, P.J., and WHITE and KELLY, JJ. 258 Mich. App. 456, 670 N.W.2d 725 (2003).
Straub v. Collette, 258 Mich. App. 456, 670 N.W.2d 725, 2003 Mich. App. LEXIS 2248 (2003)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, individuals, sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which found in favor of plaintiffs, two individuals, and reversed the trial court's grant of summary disposition in favor of defendants, holding that plaintiffs failed to prove that they suffered a serious impairment of body function pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 500.3135(1).


OVERVIEW: In two consolidated cases, the supreme court granted leave to appeal to consider whether plaintiffs satisfied the "serious impairment of body function" threshold set by the no-fault insurance act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 500.3101, et seq., in order to be able to maintain an action for noneconomic tort damages pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 500.3135(1). The trial courts granted defendants' motions for summary disposition, concluding that neither plaintiff had suffered a "serious impairment of body function," but the appellate court reversed. The supreme court reversed that decision and reinstated the trial court's order, stating that neither plaintiff satisfied the "serious impairment of body function" threshold. The specific issue was whether plaintiffs' impairments affected their general ability to lead their normal lives. In regard to the first plaintiff, the supreme court stated that there was no medical evidence that he had any residual impairment or that the course of his life had been affected. Further, while the second plaintiff could not work to full capacity, he was generally able to lead his normal life.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the appellate court's decision.

 

141 of 1632 DOCUMENTS


Grossman v. Brown


No. 122458


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


470 Mich. 593; 685 N.W.2d 198; 2004 Mich. LEXIS 1541


November 13, 2003, Argued  
July 20, 2004, Decided  
July 20, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wayne Circuit Court, Kaye Tertzag, J., Court of Appeals, TALBOT, P.J., and WILDER and MURRAY, JJ. (Docket No. 242241). Supreme Court.
Grossman v. Brown, 2002 Mich. App. LEXIS 2420 (Mich. Ct. App., Sept. 12, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff survivor sued defendant hospital and defendant physician, alleging that the physician and the hospital were negligent by failing to properly evaluate decedent and by failing to properly provide postoperative care. The hospital and the physician moved for summary disposition. The trial court denied the motion. The Michigan Court of appeals denied leave for an interlocutory appeal. Review was granted.


OVERVIEW: Survivor went to the hospital to undergo an elective surgery on his carotid artery. After the surgery, decedent began to bleed heavily internally; he died two days later. The survivor filed an affidavit of merit with her medical malpractice complaint, as required by Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.2912d(1) and Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.2169. As required, the survivor's counsel researched the physician's qualifications to obtain a qualified expert witness. Counsel maintained that, when he accessed the American Medical Association's web-site, he learned that the physician was only board certified in general surgery. As a result, for the affidavit of merit, counsel obtained a physician board-certified in general surgery who specialized in vascular surgery. In their motion for summary disposition, the physician and the hospital maintained that the expert was not qualified. At the moment the affidavit of merit was being prepared, plaintiff's attorney used the resources available to him and reasonably concluded that he had a match sufficient to meet the requirements for naming an expert. The expert was qualified for this stage of the litigation.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

142 of 1632 DOCUMENTS


People v. Goldston


No. 122364


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


470 Mich. 523; 682 N.W.2d 479; 2004 Mich. LEXIS 1524


November 12, 2003, Argued  
July 15, 2004, Decided  
July 15, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wayne Circuit Court, Ulysses W. Boykin, J., Court of Appeals, HOOD, P.J., and ZAHRA, J. (KELLY, J., would have granted leave to appeal). (Docket No. 241605).
People v. Goldston, 2002 Mich. App. LEXIS 2421 (Mich. Ct. App., Aug. 29, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Circuit court's ruling suppressing evidence reversed; remanded for reinstatement of charges against defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of an order of the Wayne Circuit Court (Michigan) ruling that the search warrant affidavit issued for the search of defendant's home did not establish probable cause for the issuance of a warrant and excluding the evidence seized under Michigan's exclusionary rule, Mich. Const. 1963, art. I, § 11.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was confronted by police officers while he was carrying a firefighter's helmet and jacket. Defendant told a police officer that he was not a fireman, but was collecting money for firefighters in New York. Suspicious officers confiscated contributions given to defendant and obtained a search warrant to search his home where the search uncovered more firefighter paraphernalia, a firearm and marijuana. The state circuit court found the affidavit did not establish probable cause for the issuance of a warrant and dismissed the charges against defendant. After the appellate court denied leave to appeal, the state supreme court adopted a good-faith exception to the exclusionary rule in Michigan and reversed the state circuit court's ruling. Specifically, the state supreme court reasoned that excluding the evidence recovered in good-faith reliance on the warrant would not further the purpose of the exclusionary rule, i.e., to deter police misconduct and that adopting the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule in Michigan was consistent with the legislative intent not to place restrictions on law enforcement activity greater than those under the Fourth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The state circuit court's suppression of evidence was reversed and remanded for reinstatement of the charges against defendant.

 

143 of 1632 DOCUMENTS


Phillips v. Mirac, Inc.


No. 121831


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


470 Mich. 415; 685 N.W.2d 174; 2004 Mich. LEXIS 1506


January 13, 2004, Argued  
July 6, 2004, Decided  
July 6, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Saginaw Circuit Court, Leopold P. Borrello, J. Court of Appeals, GAGE, P.J., and HOEKSTRA, J. (METER, J., dissenting).
Phillips v. Mirac, Inc., 251 Mich. App. 586; 651 N.W.2d 437; 2002 Mich. App. LEXIS 814 (2002).



DISPOSITION: Decision of Court of Appeals affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A trial court concluded that the damage caps of Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.401(3), which capped the amount of a lessor's liability in motor vehicle leases of 30 days or less, were unconstitutional on the basis that capping damages violated the right of trial by jury found in Mich. Const. art. 1, § 14. Appellee car rental company appealed, and the Court of Appeals of Michigan reversed. Appellant estate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.401(3) unconstitutionally infringed the right of trial by jury because Mich. Const. art. I, § 14 made what the legislature attempted to do, cap damages even though a jury found that the damages were greater than the cap, unconstitutional. The Supreme Court of Michigan held that the damages cap did not offend the passenger's constitutional right of trial by jury because the amount she actually received was never within those things a jury could decide. The supreme court also found that Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.401(3) satisfied the rational basis test; it did not violate the rights granted by the Equal Protection Clause of the Michigan Constitution because the legislation was rationally related to legitimate governmental interest. The statute was obviously designed to reduce insurance costs for automobile lessors, and because costs of operations were reduced, it increased the number of providers from which Michigan consumers could choose. Because the court found that § 257.401(3) did not violate the passenger's rights under Michigan's Equal Protection Clause, it also found it did not violate her rights under Michigan's Due Process Clause.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Judgment of Court of Appeals affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed his conviction for second-degree criminal sexual conduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was being questioned by police after being advised of his Miranda rights. After he answered several questions, the police officer asked him how many times he had sex with the victim the last time he saw her. Defendant answered that he was "taking the Fifth." Questioning ceased. The trial court ruled that defendant's statement, in its entirety, was admissible. However, the statement was never introduced into evidence or referred to by the prosecution. On appeal, defendant argued that he decided not to testify based on the improper ruling by the trial court. The court noted that, had defendant testified that he told police about the incident, defendant's invocation of his right to be silent would have been admissible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.

Adair v. State


No. 121536


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


470 Mich. 105; 680 N.W.2d 386; 2004 Mich. LEXIS 1143


October 14, 2003, Argued  
June 9, 2004, Decided  
June 9, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Claim dismissed by Adair v. State, 267 Mich. App. 583, 705 N.W.2d 541, 2005 Mich. App. LEXIS 1814 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Court of Appeals, HOLBROOK, JR., P.J., and TALBOT, J. (SAAD, J., dissenting).
Adair v. State, 250 Mich. App. 691, 651 N.W.2d 393, 2002 Mich. App. LEXIS 595 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Decision of Court of Appeals affirmed in part and reversed in part; remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, taxpayers and school districts, appealed from a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan) that found their claims of inadequate funding were barred by the doctrine of res judicata, by releases executed in prior suits pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 388.1611f, or that the unfunded activities were not new or increased activities within the meaning of Mich. Const. art. 9, § 29 of the Headlee Amendment, Mich. Const. art. 9, §§ 25-34.


OVERVIEW: Mich. Const. art 9, § 29 contained two provisions requiring defendant State to adequately fund public education. Plaintiffs asserted a claim under the second provision, the "prohibition on unfunded mandates" (POUM) provision, which required the State to fund any new or increased activities. Plaintiffs filed three counts alleging increased or new activities without funding: (I) administrative rules that required new special education activities; (II) Mich. Comp. Laws § 380.1284 that required an increase annually in the hours of pupil instruction; and (III) 12 statutes and Exec. Order No. 2000-9 that required report-keeping activities. Some plaintiffs were involved in earlier suits involving special education funding. The court found that with the limited exception of certain count III claims, plaintiffs' claims were barred by res judicata or by a release and waiver executed pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 388.1611f that applied to claims and potential claims existing during the pendency of the earlier suit. The court reversed as to the finding that record-keeping requirements found in Mich. Comp. Laws § 388.1752 and Exec. Order No. 2000-9 did not impose a new or increased mandate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the court of appeals judgment that found plaintiffs' claims of inadequate funding in violation of the Headlee Amendment were barred by the doctrine of res judicata and by releases executed in prior litigation. The court reversed the finding that record-keeping requirements imposed by statute and an executive order did not impose a new or increased mandate and remanded the case for further consistent proceedings.

People v. Nutt


No. 120489


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


469 Mich. 565; 677 N.W.2d 1; 2004 Mich. LEXIS 612

April 2, 2004, Decided

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Updated Copy October 8, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Lapeer Circuit Court, Nick Holowka, J. Oakland Circuit Court, David F. Breck, J. Court of Appeals, (Docket No. 225887).
PEOPLE v. NUTT, 2001 Mich. App. LEXIS 2322 (Mich. Ct. App., Nov. 9, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Court of Appeals' decision affirmed on different grounds; remanded to trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with receiving and concealing a stolen firearm, in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.535b, and she filed a motion to dismiss the charge, contending that it constituted an improper successive prosecution. The Oakland Circuit Court (Michigan) granted the motion, but the Court of Appeals of Michigan reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case. The state supreme court granted leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in Lapeer County (Michigan) with second-degree home invasion and larceny in a building, after she told police that she participated in three burglaries that occurred in Lapeer County, and police found firearms and other items that were stolen in a cabin in Oakland County (Michigan). Defendant pled guilty to one count of second-degree home invasion in Lapeer County six days after she was charged in Oakland County with receiving and concealing a stolen firearm and filed a motion to dismiss the charge in Oakland County, arguing that a second prosecution would violate her rights under U.S. Const. amend. V and Mich. Const. art. 1, § 15. The state supreme court held that: (1) People v. White, 390 Mich. 245, 212 N.W.2d 222, was improperly decided, and it was overruling that decision and adopting the "same-elements" test that the U.S. Supreme Court adopted in its Blockburger decision; and (2) Oakland County was not barred by U.S. Const. amend. V or Mich. Const. art. 1, § 15 from prosecuting defendant for receiving and concealing a stolen firearm, as the elements of that offense and the offense of second-degree home invasion were not the same.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the intermediate appellate court's holding that defendant could be prosecuted in Oakland County for receiving and concealing a stolen firearm, albeit on different grounds.

People v. Garza


No. 123658


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


469 Mich. 431; 670 N.W.2d 662; 2003 Mich. LEXIS 2486



November 4, 2003, Decided  
November 4, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 8, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Monroe Circuit Court, William F. LaVoy, J., Court of Appeals, COOPER, P.J., and JANSEN and GAGE, JJ. (Docket No. 246549).
People v. Garza, 2003 Mich. App. LEXIS 3460 (Mich. Ct. App., Mar. 27, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty of criminal sexual conduct in the second degree and indecent exposure, Mich. Comp. Laws §§ 750.520c, 750.335a. The trial court sentenced him to a term of three to 15 years in prison. The Court of Appeals (Michigan) denied defendant's request for leave to appeal. He then filed the instant application for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: On appeal defendant claimed that the first sentence of Mich. Comp. Laws § 769.34(10) was unconstitutional as violative of the separation of powers provisions of Mich. Const. art. 3, § 2, because it allowed the judiciary to make sentencing determinations, an area defendant claimed belonged to the legislature. The court disagreed. The court held that merely stating the principle of separation of powers provided no guidance regarding which powers belonged to which branch of government. Such was within the legislature's power to do. Through § 769.34 the legislature implemented a comprehensive sentencing reform, under which it delegated various amounts of sentencing discretion to the judiciary through different statutes. The delegated authority included appellate review of sentences pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 769.34(7)-(12). The court was neither presented with nor found any persuasive argument for finding Mich. Comp. Laws § 769.34(10) unconstitutional. The court also rejected defendant's claim that the trial court abused its sentencing discretion in the instant case and noted that the 15-year sentence was set by law under Mich. Comp. Laws §§ 750.520c(2) and 769.8(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

DeRose v. DeRose


No. 121246


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


469 Mich. 320; 666 N.W.2d 636; 2003 Mich. LEXIS 1712


March 13, 2003, Argued  
July 31, 2003, Decided  
July 31, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wayne Circuit Court, Mary M. Waterstone, J. Court of Appeals, SAWYER and OWENS, JJ. (COOPER, P.J., dissenting). 249 Mich. App. 388; 643 N.W.2d 259 (2002).
DeRose v. DeRose, 249 Mich. App. 388, 643 N.W.2d 259, 2002 Mich. App. LEXIS 54 (2002).



DISPOSITION: Decision of Court of Appeals affirmed; remanded to trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandmother sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which, in response to appellee mother's challenge to a visitation order under the grandparent visitation statute, Mich. Comp. Laws § 722.27b, held that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In divorce proceedings, the mother was awarded sole legal and physical custody of the child. The paternal grandmother sought and obtained a visitation order. The court of appeals concluded that the grandparent visitation statute was unconstitutional on the basis of a United States Supreme Court decision that dealt with a somewhat similar third-party visitation statute in another state. The court affirmed, holding that the statute was constitutionally deficient, as it did not require a trial court to show deference to the decisions of fit parents regarding grandparent visitation. The due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, included a substantive component that protected the interest of parents in the care, custody, and control of their children. On the basis of their fundamental right to raise their children, parents had the right to make decisions for their children, and such decisions had to be afforded deference.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's determination of unconstitutionality and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Charter Twp. of Northville v. Northville Pub. Sch.


Docket No. 120213.


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


469 Mich. 285; 666 N.W.2d 213; 2003 Mich. LEXIS 1713


March 12, 2003, Argued  
July 31, 2003, Decided  
July 31, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Updated Copy March 10, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Wayne Circuit Court, Kathleen I. Macdonald, J. Court of Appeals, SMOLENSKI, P.J., and JANSEN and FITZGERALD, JJ., affirmed. 247 Mich. App. 178; 635 N.W.2d 508 (2001).
Charter Twp. v. Northville Pub. Sch., 247 Mich. App. 178, 635 N.W.2d 508, 2001 Mich. App. LEXIS 168 (2001).



DISPOSITION: Decision of Court of Appeals affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff township sought to enjoin the defendants public schools, superintendent, and board of education from constructing a new high school. The trial court denied a stay, but allowed plaintiff landowners to intervene. The township and the landowners moved for summary disposition, which was denied based on Mich. Comp. Laws § 380.1263(3). The Michigan Court of Appeals affirmed. The landowners' application for leave to appeal was granted.


OVERVIEW: Before beginning construction of the new high school, the board of education met with township officials to discuss the effect of local zoning ordinances on its site plan. At issue on appeal was whether local school districts, which were required to submit building plans to the state superintendent of public instruction for approval pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 380.1263(3), must also comply with township zoning and planning ordinances pursuant to the Township Zoning Act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 125.271 et seq., and the township planning act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 125.321, et seq. The supreme court concluded that the failure to join the state superintendent as a party precluded the court from resolving the claim. The Michigan Legislature vested sole and exclusive jurisdiction over school construction and site plans in the state superintendent, who had the approval authority for school construction and site plans submitted by the local school districts. This indicated an intention to immunize school districts from local ordinances, as they affected the content of a school site plan. The issue of delegation of authority was not properly before the supreme court.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment, dismissing the landowner's appeal, and vacated the portions of the appellate court's decision that addressed the issue of delegation of legislative authority.

Harvey v. State


Docket No. 121672.


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


469 Mich. 1; 664 N.W.2d 767; 2003 Mich. LEXIS 1491


April 9, 2003, Argued  
July 16, 2003, Decided  
July 16, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Updated Copy March 9, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Ingham Circuit Court, Lawrence M. Glazer, J. Court of Appeals, MCDONALD, P.J., and BANDSTRA and C. L. BOSMAN, JJ. (Docket No. 187112). Court of Appeals, FITZGERALD, P.J., and BANDSTRA and K. F. KELLY, JJ.
Harvey v. State, 251 Mich. App. 323, 650 N.W.2d 392, 2002 Mich. App. LEXIS 700 (2002)..



DISPOSITION: Decision of the Court of Appeals reversed; the original judgment of the Ingham Circuit Court reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State, the Department of Management and Budget, Bureau of Retirement Services, and Judges Retirement Board (Michigan), sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which ruled in favor of plaintiff retired state district court judges and concluded that the Judges Retirement Act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 38.2101 et seq., was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The judges asserted that the Act, specifically Mich. Comp. Laws §§ 38.2104(1)(b), (d), 38.2108(3), (8), violated the Equal Protection Clause in Mich. Const. art. I, § 2 by providing a greater retirement allowance to 36th district court judges than to all others. The appellate court applied the intermediate scrutiny test and held that the Act was unconstitutional. The court reversed. In determining the proper level of scrutiny to apply, the court determined that the present state of both federal and Michigan equal protection jurisprudence failed to support application of the intermediate scrutiny test to statutes that created a discrete exception to a general rule, where the exception was no longer considered experimental. Accordingly, the court overruled the holding of Manistee Bank v. McGowan, 394 Mich. 655 (1975), to the extent that it created the "discrete exception to a general rule" basis for applying intermediate scrutiny, but affirmed its recognition of the existence of the intermediate scrutiny test. The Act provided for the pensions of the 36th district court judges to be more secure. Thus, the Act and the contested provisions were deemed constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision and reinstated the trial court's judgment in defendants' favor.

People v. Hawkins


No. 120437, No. 121698


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


468 Mich. 488; 668 N.W.2d 602; 2003 Mich. LEXIS 1728


December 11, 2002, Argued  
June 20, 2003, Decided  
June 20, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
People v. Hawkins, 654 N.W.2d 329, 2002 Mich. LEXIS 1906 (Mich., 2002)
People v. Scherf, 251 Mich. App. 410, 651 N.W.2d 77, 2002 Mich. App. LEXIS 720 (2002)



DISPOSITION:  Hawkins, reversed and remanded to the Court of Appeals. Scherf, reversed and remanded to the district-court division of the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Michigan) affirmed a circuit court's grant of a motion to suppress evidence obtained through a search warrant obtained in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 780.653 in pretrial proceedings against defendant one. The Court of Appeals also affirmed a circuit court's reversal of a district court's denial of defendant two's motion to suppress evidence based on a violation of Mich. Ct. R. 3.606. The State appealed both judgments.


OVERVIEW: In defendant one's case, the affidavit for a search warrant did not meet the requirements of Mich. Comp. Laws § 780.653(B) because it did not include information concerning the credibility of the unnamed informants or the reliability of the information they supplied. In defendant's two's case, the circuit court held that although the failure to provide an affidavit with a bench warrant petition for defendant two's arrest was merely technical, it rendered the bench warrant invalid. Without addressing the constitutionality of the warrants, on appeal the court addressed only whether the exclusionary rule was properly applied to evidence seized in each case and held that the mere technical violations at issue did not mandate application of the exclusionary rule. Neither the statute nor the rule at issue specifically stated that such violations required exclusion of evidence obtained under the warrants. Additionally, the court held that applying the rule would not further the purpose of deterring wrongful police conduct because in both cases the officers had acted in good faith in obtaining the warrants.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the intermediate appellate court's judgment in both cases. Regarding defendant one's case, the court remanded to matter to the intermediate appellate court to address the State's additional arguments on appeal. Regarding defendant two's case, the court remanded the matter to the district court division for further proceedings. The court did not retain jurisdiction.
